### Beyond Borders Gazette (@bb_gazette)
_Fri Jun 05 17:20:06 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/bb_gazette/status/2062947584742920575)

> Researchers at Monash University have developed a tiny chip that could help pave the way for computers that process information using light instead of electricity. Published in the journal Nature Photonics, the study demonstrates a nanoscale device capable of generating, controlling and reading light-based signals on a single platform. The breakthrough uses an emerging technology called valleytronics, which relies on quantum properties in advanced materials to encode information. Researchers say the innovation could lead to faster computing, lower energy consumption and more efficient communication systems in the future.
>
> Investigadores de la Universidad Monash desarrollaron un diminuto chip que podría ayudar a abrir el camino hacia computadoras capaces de procesar información utilizando luz en lugar de electricidad. Publicado en la revista Nature Photonics, el estudio demuestra un dispositivo a escala nanométrica capaz de generar, controlar y leer señales basadas en luz en una sola plataforma. El avance utiliza una tecnología emergente conocida como valleytrónica, que aprovecha propiedades cuánticas de materiales avanzados para codificar información. Los investigadores afirman que la innovación podría conducir a una computación más rápida, un menor consumo de energía y sistemas de comunicación más eficientes en el futuro.
>
> #Chip #Information #Light #TechInvestigation #valleytronics

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKEP5I_bEAA66WO.jpg

### SailorSBG (@NucSBG)
_Fri Jun 05 17:20:55 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/NucSBG/status/2062947792008413666)

> ============================================================
> SOLIDIFICATION OF LIGHT AND PROGRAMMABLE MATTER
> Connection Brief
> ============================================================
>
> Solidification of Light:
> - Refers to experiments making photons behave like condensed matter.
> - Key breakthrough (March 2025): Italian researchers created the first
>   "photonic supersolid" — light that has a rigid crystalline structure
>   (solid-like) while flowing without friction (superfluid-like).
> - Achieved using exciton-polaritons in semiconductor nanostructures.
>
> Programmable Matter:
> - Materials that can change physical properties (shape, density,
>   optical traits, stiffness) in a controlled/programmable way.
> - Includes metamaterials, shape-changing systems, and modular robotics.
>
> Connections:
> 1. Light as a programmable medium: Supersolid light and polariton
>    systems allow dynamic, reconfigurable quantum states controlled
>    by lasers or external fields.
>
> 2. Programmable photonics overlap: Solid-light phenomena can serve
>    as building blocks for adaptive optical chips, tunable lasers,
>    optical neural networks, and quantum simulators.
>
> 3. Hybrid future tech: Combines exotic quantum behavior of "solid"
>    light with the reconfigurability of smart materials, enabling
>    potential applications in quantum computing, adaptive optics,
>    and light-based programmable devices.
>
> Current status: Mostly laboratory-scale quantum experiments, but
> strong conceptual bridge toward future smart photonic materials.
>
> References:
> [1] Live Science / Nature (2025) - Photonic supersolid creation
> [2] Wikipedia / ScienceAlert - Solid light and supersolids
> [3] Wikipedia - Programmable matter
> [4] Related works on polaritons and programmable photonics

### Piggo’s Trading Desk (@Piggos_T_Desk)
_Fri Jun 05 17:23:44 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 4 · ↻ 2 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/Piggos_T_Desk/status/2062948497977196803)

> 🚨 Photonics may become the most important technology shift of the next decade.
>
> Not AI software.
>
> Not apps.
>
> Not even GPUs alone.
>
> The REAL revolution may be the replacement of electricity with LIGHT inside computing infrastructure. 🧵
>
> Silicon electronics are approaching physical limits.
>
> Modern AI infrastructure now faces: ⚠️ bandwidth ceilings ⚠️ power-consumption explosions ⚠️ heat-density problems ⚠️ latency bottlenecks ⚠️ interconnect saturation
>
> The current architecture is becoming unsustainable.
>
> This is where photonics enters.
>
> Photonics = using LIGHT (photons) instead of electricity (electrons) to: 💡 transmit data 💡 process signals 💡 move information 💡 scale compute infrastructure
>
> The implications are enormous.
>
> We believe photonics is no longer speculative science fiction.
>
> It is increasingly becoming: ⚠️ necessary ⚠️ commercially viable ⚠️ strategically essential
>
> Especially for hyperscale AI systems.
>
> The AI boom itself is creating the problem photonics solves.
>
> As models scale: 📈 compute demand explodes 📈 rack density rises 📈 cooling loads surge 📈 electricity consumption skyrockets
>
> Copper interconnects increasingly become the bottleneck.
>
> Traditional electrical systems waste massive amounts of energy as heat.
>
> Photonics changes the equation: ⚡ lower power consumption ⚡ faster transmission ⚡ lower latency ⚡ higher bandwidth ⚡ less thermal stress
>
> This is why hyperscalers are aggressively pursuing it.
>
> In this case the sequence is straightforward:
>
> Step 1: 🤖 AI models scale exponentially
>
> Step 2: ⚠️ Electrical interconnects hit limits
>
> Step 3: 🔥 Cooling and power costs explode
>
> Step 4: 💡 Photonics becomes economically necessary
>
> Step 5: 🏗 Entire data-center architecture changes
>
> This transition is already happening quietly.
>
> Over the next 3–5 years: ⚠️ co-packaged optics ⚠️ optical switching ⚠️ silicon photonics ⚠️ photonic networking
>
> …will increasingly replace traditional copper infrastructure.
>
> The implications go far beyond performance.
>
> Photonics may fundamentally reshape: 🏭 semiconductor design ⚡ power consumption 💧 cooling infrastructure 🧠 AI deployment economics 🏢 hyperscale construction
>
> We believe this becomes one of the clearest examples of K-shaped technological consolidation.
>
> Why?
>
> Because only the largest players can afford: 💰 photonic R&D 💰 custom AI infrastructure 💰 advanced packaging 💰 optical integration (Watch chip makers rotating, new partnerships)
>
> Smaller competitors increasingly get locked out.
>
> The photonics transition favors: ✅ hyperscalers ✅ mega-cap semiconductor firms ✅ defense-linked infrastructure players ✅ vertically integrated ecosystems
>
> The technological moat widens.
>
> 🚨 INVESTABLE PLAYERS
>
> Several companies already sit directly inside this transition.
>
> ⚡ Broadcom ($AVGO) ⚡ Coherent ($COHR) ⚡ Lumentum ($LITE) ⚡ Intel ($INTC) ⚡ Laser Photonics ($LASE)
>
> Each attacks a different layer of the stack.
>
> $AVGO is one of the strongest large-cap photonics plays.
>
> Broadcom already dominates: 🔌 networking 🔌 optical connectivity 🔌 silicon-photonics infrastructure 🔌 AI data-center interconnects
>
> It sits directly at the AI bandwidth bottleneck.
>
> $COHR is another critical player.
>
> Coherent controls: 💡 industrial lasers 💡 optical subsystems 💡 photonic components 💡 semiconductor manufacturing optics
>
> As photonic infrastructure scales, laser demand scales with it.
>
> $LITE remains deeply leveraged to: 📡 fiber optics 📡 telecom photonics 📡 optical sensing 📡 AI networking expansion
>
> The company effectively monetizes bandwidth growth itself.
>
> $INTC is quietly positioning aggressively in silicon photonics.
>
> Intel understands a critical reality:
>
> Traditional scaling alone is no longer enough.
>
> Future compute increasingly depends on: 💡 optical movement of data rather than purely electrical scaling.
>
> Smaller pure-play names like: ⚡ $LASE ⚡ Ayar Labs (private) ⚡ Lightmatter (private)
>
> represent the more speculative frontier.
>
> Higher risk. Potentially enormous upside.
>
> Especially if optical interconnect adoption accelerates faster than expected.
>
> Emphasis
>
> In photonics the bottlenecks are: ⚠️ optical integration ⚠️ laser systems ⚠️ advanced packaging ⚠️ thermal efficiency ⚠️ networking infrastructure
>
> The defense angle matters enormously too.
>
> Photonics is not just about AI chatbots.
>
> It increasingly affects: 🛰 satellite systems 🎯 targeting infrastructure 📡 radar systems ⚔ electronic warfare 🤖 autonomous drones
>
> This is becoming strategic infrastructure.
>
> Another major theme:
>
> Photonics helps reduce energy intensity.
>
> This becomes critical because hyperscale AI now collides directly with: ⚡ grid shortages 💧 water scarcity 🔥 cooling constraints 🛢 diesel stress
>
> The physical economy increasingly constrains digital expansion.
>
> We have repeatedly emphasized:
>
> The future AI race may not simply be about: “Who has the best model?”
>
> It may become: “Who can physically power and cool computation?”
>
> Photonics helps solve that problem.
>
> This is why the market increasingly rewards: 🏗 infrastructure ⚡ utilities 💧 cooling 🧲 critical minerals 💡 photonic efficiency
>
> The AI story is becoming deeply industrial.
>
> The broader implication is profound:
>
> Photonics may ultimately do to traditional electronics… …what the internet did to analog communication.
>
> The infrastructure layer itself changes.
>
> But the transition also accelerates concentration.
>
> Only a narrowing circle of: 🏢 hyperscalers 🏦 mega-cap firms 🏭 industrial suppliers ⚔ defense-linked infrastructure players
>
> …may fully benefit.
>
> The K-shape deepens.
>
> The irony is striking:
>
> The AI revolution was originally marketed as democratizing technology.
>
> Instead it increasingly centralizes: ⚡ compute ⚡ infrastructure ⚡ capital ⚡ energy access ⚡ photonic capability
>
> into fewer hands.
>
> We believe the market still underestimates how quickly photonics may become unavoidable.
>
> Because the problem is no longer theoretical.
>
> The electrical system itself is hitting physical limits.
>
> The final takeaway:
>
> The next generation of AI winners may not simply be software companies.
>
> They may be the firms controlling: 💡 light transmission ⚡ power efficiency 🔥 thermal management 🏗 optical infrastructure
>
> The future of computing increasingly belongs to photonics.
>

### Andiamo (@andiamonow)
_Fri Jun 05 19:35:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 261 · ↻ 39 · 💬 12 · [open on X](https://x.com/andiamonow/status/2062981542767407527)

> 🚨 CONFIRMED via Finansinspektionen (Swedish FSA): JPMorgan Chase & Co. just crossed the 5% ownership threshold in $SIVE.
>
> Official filing:
> → Holder: JPMorgan Chase & Co.
> → Transaction date: June 2, 2026 (same day as the GlobalFoundries announcement)
> → Reason for flagging: "Köp" (BUY)
> → Pre-transaction position: 0 shares
> → Post-transaction position: 16,098,583 shares / 5.25008% of total voting rights
>
> Position structure:
> → J.P. Morgan Securities plc (UK entity): 15,916,852 voting rights — 5.19%
> → J.P. Morgan Securities LLC (US entity): 181,731 voting rights — 0.06%
> → Direct shares: 10,049,558 (3.14% of total shares)
> → Cash-settled instruments (likely swaps): 6,049,025 share equivalents
>
> Why this is structurally significant:
>
> Swedish law requires mandatory disclosure when crossing the 5% ownership threshold. JPMorgan went from ZERO to 5.25% on June 2. The flagging reason filed with the FSA was explicitly "Köp" (Buy) — not custody, not market-making inventory. This is a deliberate institutional position.
>
> The timing is what makes it remarkable:
>
> June 2 was the same day GlobalFoundries announced the silicon photonics reference design partnership and $SIVE moved +50-70%.
>
> Three possible reads:
> JPM was positioned beforehand and captured the move
>
> JPM built the position aggressively into and after the news.
>
> JPM is positioning ahead of the Nasdaq NY listing in an underwriter / placement agent role
>
> All three are bullish. The third would be the most strategically significant — tier-1 US investment banks don't take 5% positions in Swedish micro-caps without strategic context.
>
> Connecting back to the "zero institutional ownership" post earlier this week:
>
> Five days ago: $SIVE had zero US institutional 13F filings.
>
> Today: the world's largest investment bank discloses a 5%+ position triggered by a "Buy" transaction.
>
> The institutional layer that was missing has started forming.
> The composition tells you it's sophisticated:
> 6 million of the 16 million share-equivalents are in cash-settled derivatives. The rest is direct shares. This is the kind of structured position you set up when you're a major capital markets player preparing for a multi-event sequence — index inclusions, dual listing, sector rotation.
>
> JPMorgan doesn't take 5% positions in $2-3B Swedish micro-caps because they're bored.
>
> $SIVE just got its first major Wall Street institutional anchor.
>
> $SIVE

### Data Fondamental (@datafondamental)
_Fri Jun 05 21:26:30 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/datafondamental/status/2063009594348130317)

> #AnalyseAction - Sivers Semiconductors (SIVE)
>
> On en parle énormément en ce moment, plus haut historique à 110 SEK le 3 juin, environ +60% sur la semaine. Mais déjà deux grosses séances de baisse : -9% hier, encore -9% aujourd'hui à la clôture. On pose les chiffres avant de suivre le momentum.
>
> Le profil :
> Small cap suédoise (Stockholm), spécialiste des réseaux de lasers pour l'optique intégrée des datacenters IA. Cœur de la thèse : la bascule du cuivre vers l'optique (CPO).
>
> Les chiffres (5 juin : 78,80 SEK) :
> Capi ~23 Md SEK. 
> CA 2025 : 360,8 M SEK (+33%). 
> Résultat net : -186,5 M SEK, marge -52%. P/S ~83x. 
> Pas de dividende. Une boîte valorisée plus de 80 fois ses ventes, et pas rentable.
>
> Pourquoi ça flambe (et pourquoi ça corrige) ?
> Deux catalyseurs réels : l'extension du partenariat avec Ayar Labs (lasers Sivers dans la source SuperNova) et la collaboration toute fraîche avec GlobalFoundries, qui intègre ses lasers dans ses designs de référence silicon photonics. Validation par un fondeur majeur, c'est du concret. À noter, certains arguments avancés par @aleabitoreddit sur le rôle de chokepoint laser de Sivers sont d'ailleurs assez intéressants sur le fond. Mais après un tel run, la moindre prise de bénéfices fait très mal, d'où les deux séances rouges.
>
> La cotation à New York :
> Sivers évalue une double cotation au Nasdaq New York (annoncée le 16 avril), tout en gardant son siège en Suède. Ça impose une mise à niveau comptable aux normes PCAOB, dont la certification serait le dernier obstacle avant l'entrée au Nasdaq. Vrai catalyseur potentiel (liquidité, base d'investisseurs US). 
>
> Réserve importante : l'autorité suédoise enquête sur un possible délit d'initié lié à la fuite du projet via un compte anonyme. Tant que ce nuage n'est pas levé, il pèse sur le titre.
>
> Le point noir des résultats :
> T1 2026 : CA en baisse de 22% sur un an. Mais pipeline d'opportunités à 799 M$ (+77% depuis fin 2025) et production LiDAR prévue au T4. Le CA recule pendant que la promesse grossit. Toute la valo repose sur la conversion de ce pipeline.
>
> Mon avis :
> Bonne boîte, meilleur thème du cycle actuel, mais valo déconnectée du présent et risque réglementaire ouvert. Le profil qui peut continuer à monter sur le momentum et corriger violemment au premier accroc (deux séances à -9% d'affilée le rappellent). 
>
> Transparence : j'en détiens, et je l'achète directement sur la bourse suédoise en SEK (et non via l'OTC US). Et c'est pour ça que je m'oblige à rester lucide. À ce prix, j'achète une histoire et un calendrier de catalyseurs, pas des fondamentaux.
>
> Et vous, vous jouez la cotation US et le pipeline, ou la valo et le risque vous semblent intenables ?
>
> Ceci n'est en aucun cas un conseil en investissement, faites vos propres recherches.

### Ryan sikorski (@Ryansikorski10)
_Fri Jun 05 22:02:42 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 17 · ↻ 7 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/Ryansikorski10/status/2063018701931134996)

> HIGH–PULSE-ENERGY FEMTOSECOND MODE-LOCKED LASERS FOR ON CHIP OPTICAL AMPLIFICATION
>
> Over the past decades, extensive efforts have been devoted to developing photonic integrated circuit-based mode-locked lasers that are compact, scalable, and compatible with further on-chip functionalities. Yet, existing implementations fall short of pulse energies required for their subsequent uses in nonlinear applications. THE FIRST MODE-LOCKED LASER THAT OVERCOMES THIS LIMITATION IN LOW-LOSS ERBIUM-DOPED SILICON NITRIDE PHOTONIC INTEGRATED CIRCUITS.
>
> On-chip optical amplification
>
> Because the need for faster chips is expected to see a shift from electronics- to photonics-based technologies, erbium ions could form the basis for amplification in optical integrated circuits. We apply ion implantation to ultralow–loss silicon nitride (Si3N4) photonic integrated circuits, WHICH ARE ABLE TO INCREASE THE SOLITON MICROCOMB OUTPUT POWER BY 100 TIMES, achieving power requirements for low-noise photonic microwave generation and wavelength-division multiplexing optical communications. 
>
> OPERATING IN THE CONTINUOUS-WAVE REGIME and PROVIDING LARGE OPTICAL GAIN IN THE TELECOMMUNICATION BANDS, the results are promising for device (human) applications. —ISO
>
> Endowing Si3N4 photonic integrated circuits WITH GAIN ENABLES THE MINIATURIZATION OF VARIOUS FIBER-BASED DEVICES such as HIGH–PULSE-ENERGY FEMTOSECOND MODE-LOCKED LASERS.
>
> https://t.co/YQyK4yDqj8
>
> The laser is based on the Mamyshev oscillator architecture [8, 9],https://t.co/sgQSd01Yzd which employs alternating spectral filtering & self-phase modulation for mode-locking. It delivers a 176 MHz stream of pulses w/ nanojoule energy, comparable to fiber lasers & surpassing previous photonic integrated sources by more than two orders of magnitude. The output pulses exhibit excellent coherence, can be linearly compressed to 147 fs & directly drive a 1.5-octave-spanning supercontinuum in an integrated waveguide. 
>
> https://t.co/aQKEw7b6le

### くえるじゃん (@Kuerujan)
_Fri Jun 05 23:58:52 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 1 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/Kuerujan/status/2063047935626276996)

> AI半導体投資日報_260606_朝刊
>
> ■朝刊の見取り図
> ・前回夕刊以降の更新で一番重要なのは、AI半導体の実需が強いまま、株価、電力、資源、政策、企業AI ROIの側で検証圧力が上がったこと。
> ・NVIDIA Vera Rubin向けHBM4では、Samsung Electronics、SK hynix、Micronが認定済みで生産中と報じられた。
> ・BroadcomのAI売上は強い。それでも半導体株は急落した。市場は需要の有無ではなく、期待値、金利、長期target、粗利率、顧客集中を見た。
> ・AIデータセンターは、電力、水、土地、冷却、microgrid、費用回収の問題として扱う必要が強まった。
> ・台湾、韓国掲示板、欧州政策の細い観測点は、価値配分がGPU/HBMだけに閉じないことを補強した。
> ・朝刊の結論は明確。AI需要は消えていない。投資では、強い実需をそのまま高リターンへ変換せず、供給制約、導入制約、価格転嫁、織り込み度を分けて確認する。
>
> ■HBM4三社認定は供給リスク低下だが、配分は未確定
> ・NVIDIA CEO Jensen Huangが、Vera Rubin向けHBM4でSamsung Electronics、SK hynix、Micronの三社がqualifiedでproduction中と述べたと報じられた。
> ・この材料は、Vera Rubin世代のHBM4供給網が単一サプライヤー依存から三社体制へ広がる確認材料である。NVIDIA側には、ramp時の供給選択肢と価格交渉余地が増える。
> ・一方で、公式なvolume allocation、層数、容量、速度、電圧、歩留まり、ASP、LTA条件は未開示である。SK hynix、Samsung、Micronの収益配分をこの報道だけで定量化しない。
> ・HBM4の供給力は、DRAM stackだけで決まらない。base die、TSV、bonding、test、CoWoS/2.5D能力、interposer、基板、液冷、電源、ラック組立が同時に必要になる。
> ・投資では、HBM4認定をメモリ企業の強気材料として見る。同時に、NVIDIAの調達分散が将来の価格交渉、HBM5移行、通常DRAM wafer配分へどう効くかを追う。
>
> ■Broadcom後の急落は需要減速ではなく期待値調整
> ・Reutersは、Broadcom決算後に米国上場チップメーカーの時価総額が大きく消え、PHLX Semiconductor Indexも急落したと報じた。
> ・重要なのは、BroadcomのAI半導体売上が弱かったわけではない点である。BroadcomのAI semiconductor revenueは高成長を続けている。
> ・市場が見たのは、7月期ガイダンス、2027年AI revenue target据え置き、custom AI chip需要の上振れ余地、粗利率、顧客集中、金利上昇による評価倍率の圧縮である。
> ・これはAI半導体テーマの弱気転換ではない。強い決算でも、事前期待がさらに高い場合は株価が下がる。AI株は実需テーマであると同時に、遠い将来利益を織り込む長期成長株である。
> ・確認すべき指標は、AI acceleratorとAI networkingの内訳、主要顧客、gross margin、HBM/CoWoS/基板制約、クラウド側のcapex回収、AIアプリ側の売上化である。
>
> ■AIデータセンターは電力・水・土地で稼働能力が決まる
> ・Axiosの記事は、AIデータセンターの制約を電力だけでなく、水、土地、e-waste、冷却、地域負担へ広げた。
> ・DOE Office of Electricityの記事は、AIデータセンターや先端産業の大口負荷に対して、microgrid、stand-alone bridge、grid-connected support、蓄電、需要応答、費用回収が重要になることを示した。
> ・DOEは、データセンター電力使用量が2014年の58TWhから2023年の176TWhへ増え、2028年には325TWhから580TWhへ増える見通しも示した。単一サイトが最大4.5GWを要求する例もある。
> ・この論点は半導体需要に二面で効く。系統接続や地域合意が遅れれば、GPU/HBM出荷がクラウド売上へ変わる時期は後ろ倒しになる。一方で、変圧器、ケーブル、蓄電、microgrid制御、冷却、水処理、電力ソフトウェアには新しい需要が生まれる。
> ・データセンターcapexを読むときは、チップ発注だけでなく、接続時期、電源構成、PUE/WUE、地域許認可、料金負担、負荷柔軟性を同じ画面で確認する。
>
> ■台湾・韓国・欧州の細い材料が価値配分を広げる
> ・Taipei Timesは、TSMC C.C. WeiのAI需要発言を、先端チップ、装置、装置部品、メモリ、packaging、testing、cooling systems、power supplyの同時制約として伝えた。
> ・TWSE/COMPUTEX記事では、Nanya、Alchip、Unimicron、Msscorps関連発言が、DRAM bit growth、custom AI chip、ABF substrate、packaging materials、materials analysisへ需要を分解した。
> ・DCInsideのSoCAMM投稿は、Rubin NVL72の容量縮小観測を、メモリ容量減少ではなくmodule count、substrate specification、rack shipmentで読む視点を示した。掲示板材料のため、公式仕様と部品表の確認が必要である。
> ・Bits&ChipsのEU Chips Act 2.0記事は、欧州政策が前工程fab偏重から、需要側施策、成熟半導体、設計、3D packaging、装置、specialty materials、integrated photonicsへ広がると整理した。
> ・EvertiqのTessalia記事は、Foxconn、Radiall、ThalesのフランスSiP拠点を、高信頼実装、防衛、通信、医療向けの主権能力形成として位置づける材料である。AIサーバー直結ではないが、欧州の後工程政策を見る入口になる。
>
> ■企業AIのROIは半導体需要の反証条件になる
> ・THE DECODERが紹介したBain調査では、AI cost savingsを測定した企業の約40%が10%未満の削減にとどまった。一方で、9割の企業はAI投資を増やす計画を持つ。
> ・この材料はAIブームの否定ではない。企業はAIをやめていない。問題は、agent導入が人間の承認、データアクセス、監査、権限管理、業務設計で詰まることにある。
> ・CloudflareのVoidZero買収は、AI codingがモデルAPIだけでなく、Vite、build、test、Workers、D1、R2、edge deployment、intent-based infrastructureへ需要を広げる観測点である。
> ・ユーザー提供資料のAIバブル論は、技術失速ではなく、鉄道バブル型の回収時期ずれ、航空業界型の価格競争、用途別棲み分け、先行者優位プロダクトの有無を論点にした。
> ・半導体側の受注が強くても、最終需要側のROIが広く確認できなければ、クラウドcapexとモデル企業の投資回収は脆くなる。逆にROIが確認されれば、推論需要は一段長く続く。
>
> ■朝刊の確認ポイント
> ・HBM4は、認定済みという事実と、配分・歩留まり・ASP未確認を分ける。
> ・Broadcom後の急落は、実需減速ではなく期待値、金利、粗利率、顧客集中の検証として扱う。
> ・AIデータセンターは、GPU/HBM発注と稼働開始を分け、電力、水、土地、地域合意、microgridを追う。
> ・台湾・韓国・欧州材料は、ABF、SoCAMM、packaging materials、materials analysis、SiP、integrated photonicsへ価値連鎖を広げる。
> ・企業AIは、agent発表よりも、data access、human-in-the-loop、監査、task completion、顧客ROIで見る。

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HKFrKbcbQAAqmHP.jpg

### charahim94 (@charahim9494)
_Sat Jun 06 20:54:08 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/charahim9494/status/2063363833867985261)

> TSMC’s COUPE™ platform is one to watch.

### NMSI - Subquantum Physics (@PCosmologist)
_Sat Jun 06 21:51:03 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 3 · ↻ 2 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/PCosmologist/status/2063378160474095892)

> This is the kind of breakthrough that could completely transform:
> sensing;
> photonics;
> and AI–environment interfaces.
> The truly revolutionary aspect is not just: “a spectrometer on a chip,”
> but the fact that: the material structure itself becomes: an optical processor.
> In practice: plastic is no longer just a passive substrate.
> It becomes: geometrically programmed matter for light processing.
> What is especially interesting is that: the laser-induced micro-vortices create: local phase and interference structures.
>
> Within NMSI, this is highly relevant, because it strongly resembles:
> phase routing;
> resonant nodes;
> and distributed coherent processing.
> Such structures could become extremely valuable for: GPU Coherent:
> integrated optical sensors;
> local spectral feedback;
> phase monitoring;
> and ultra-compact coherent readout.
> In practice: matter is beginning: not just to transport light, but: to structurally “interpret” it.

### Michael Sikand 🦑 (@michaelsikand)
_Sat Jun 06 22:29:05 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 336 · ↻ 13 · 💬 39 · [open on X](https://x.com/michaelsikand/status/2063387729359208809)

> My highest conviction thesis this decade.
>
> The investment research industry for retail investors (FinX, Substack etc.) is going to 10x fast.
>
> And it's regardless of what the market ultimately does this decade.
>
> Currently the market for institutional sell side research is estimated at ~$13.7B globally. 
>
> Now look at the mix from retail in the market itself.
>
> Retail was 10% of US equity volume in 2010. 15% before COVID. In 2025 it's averaging 20-25% and it spiked north of 35% in April, an all time high per JPMorgan.
>
> So if a third of all the capital hitting the market is retail and that market keeps growing?
>
> That $13.7B research machine spends $0 advising 1/3 of the investor base aside from PTs they pull out without sharing ANY of their modelling.
>
> Goldman isn't using their teams of Harvard grads to share the 2030 photonics TAM with retail.
>
> So where does retail get its information? Right now, I see it as an insanely underserved market.
>
> The status quo for retail is mostly slop articles generated by the big websites like Motley Fool and Yahoo farming SEO traffic giving 0 alpha.
>
> The good stuff?
>
> - There's a couple of Substacks probably doing 8 figures. Maybe a few dozen doing 7 figs at most.
>
> -  On FinX, there's a handful of maybe 20 influential X accounts (call it a few M followers combined) sharing actually high quality equity research.
>
> This is peanuts. If 70% of the global capital right now is serviced by a $13B annual industry.
>
> And FinX/Substack is only generating low hundreds of millions? 
>
> How can it not 10x here shortly as retail grows in influence and power?
>

### M T (@mtaaafm)
_Sat Jun 06 22:32:00 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/mtaaafm/status/2063388466076099066)

> Think about electricity.
>
> The biggest winners of electrification weren’t necessarily the companies making appliances.
>
> Many fortunes were made by the companies building the infrastructure: power plants, transmission lines, transformers, and industrial equipment.
>
> AI may follow the same path.
>
> If AI usage grows 10x–100x over the next decade, the world will need:
>
> • More GPUs
> • More memory
> • More networking
> • More photonics
> • More servers
> • More data centers
> • More power generation
> • More cooling systems
> • More AI cloud capacity
> • More AI infrastructure management
>
> The reason some AI infrastructure companies trade at high valuations today is because investors believe today’s infrastructure is still far too small for future demand.
>
> The biggest winners may not be the companies using AI.
>
> They may be the companies enabling AI to scale.
> #AI #Investing

### Enkhmanal 🟠 (@Enkhmanal)
_Sat Jun 06 22:49:24 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Enkhmanal/status/2063392842807194040)

> $GLW - NVIDIA IS PAYING CORNING TO REPLACE COPPER WITH GLASS INSIDE THE AI RACK
> Corning's multiyear pact commits Nvidia to invest up to $3.2B — including $500M of warrants — to 10x Corning's US optical-connectivity capacity and lift US fiber output more than 50% across three new plants. The pull: Nvidia's Spectrum-X Ethernet Photonics, its first co-packaged-optics switch, entered production May 31, and CPO swaps copper cabling for glass fiber from rack down to the chip.
> The mechanism: CPO doesn't kill optical content, it moves the dollars from the pluggable module into the fiber layer Corning owns — a structural socket the Friday selloff treated as just another chip-beta name.

> Hey chat, let me put some respect on $ALRIB 🧵
>
> Riber SA. French semi equipment maker. ~€300M market cap. 109 employees. global leader in MBE — the process used to grow semiconductor layers inside quantum dot lasers, photonics chips, and AI data center components.
>
> You've never heard of them. that's the point.
> The numbers→ revenue €40.3M, net income €5.2M, margin 13% → order book up 24% to €26.9M end of 2025 → fresh Japan production order in Jan 2026 (not even in the book yet)
>
> ROSIE is the real thesis - Their new platform for silicon-based integrated photonics, compatible with 300mm production lines. first two units ordered in 2025. ROSIE 2 (dual-chamber) in production in 2026.
>
> This is the format hyperscalers need. 300mm compatibility = plug into existing fab infrastructure. that's not a research tool. that's an industrial product entering a massive market.
>
> Why it's undervalued - Every quantum dot laser in every AI data center optical link needs MBE - Riber is the global leader in that equipment. 
> One company : 109 people, €300M market cap. analyst target still €6. stock at €15.70. analysts haven't moved since the AI photonics cycle started.
>
> Upcoming catalyst June 17 shareholder meeting. €0.10/share cash distribution (+25%) proposed, payable June 24. Profitable company returning cash while deploying next-gen tech. 
>
> This is what undervalued looks like before the market figures it out.

>
> ✅ AI tạo ra lượng dữ liệu khổng lồ

>

### The Observer (@TheObserverCap)

> Decided to size up a bit on my #1 favourite stock last week.
>
> After enjoying the gains in photonics and memory earlier this year with $SOI (entered at €48), $AAOI (entered at $47) and $MU (entered at $338), I've moved on to just $EOS.AX. ($GP6 is the European ticker of $EOS.AX, for diversification purposes)
>
> EOS is becoming a full stack air defense prime. They offer sensors, AI command and control (MARSS NiDAR), kinetic effectors (RWS, interceptor drones, rocket and missile systems), and directed-energy lasers (Apollo 100 kW today, 300 kW C-RAM in development). The kill chain is combat proven in Ukraine and Iran, the order book is at an inflection point. The market still treats it like a niche Australian small cap rather than the global defense prime it's turning into.
>
> AI / Photonics / Memory is starting to feel a little hot after a huge run, where the reward doesn't justify the risk for me personally. Defense stocks are still beaten down, even after their jump following the Trump investment news. 
>
> Especially C-UAS focused stocks, after the Iran conflict exposed how unprepared the West still is, are structurally underappreciated. The US has spent billions on million-dollar Patriot and SM-2 interceptors trying to shoot down $20-50K Shahed drones, a cost equation that simply cannot scale. 
>
> The Australian market has lagged the S&P 500 too, and if a deal with Iran is actually close it should benefit Australia a lot. I also believe that the next 6-12 months should bring the contract conversions that force a rerate in the stock: massive Apollo lasers, MARSS and RWS orders worth multiple billions of dollars. I expect Europe and the Middle East to be major customers in the near future.

### John Galt (@AtlasShrug1)
_Sun May 31 19:25:33 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 9 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AtlasShrug1/status/2061167216188371068)

> Those 2 things are not mutually exclusive.  I would say based on my analysis that it a solid company, though much of the move to photonics and power semis will take a long time, that is a small % of rhe mix rn.  You have mostly auto and industrial exposure.  
>
> The point I want to make though is a bigger one.  You have to look at the stock separate from the company because there is one other key variable, the price you pay.  A Ferarri is a great car isnt it?  But would you pay $10 million for on?  Probably no, even id you could afford it.   
>
> You can make money buying mediocre companies and prices that bake in them being horrible companies. You can make money buying great companies when they are priced reasonably relative to their future growth prospects.  
>
> Entry point is the key.  If you massively overpay for an asset, be it a middling one or a trophy asset, it may take a decade to recover from that mistake.

### Drabone hoo (@bizihaosuan)
_Sun May 31 21:59:48 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/bizihaosuan/status/2061206035533267417)

> Sivers Semiconductors Q1 是个很适合校准 CPO / optical interconnect 交易的例子。
>
> 公司 Q1 net sales 61.9 MSEK，同比 -22%；Photonics revenue 17.8 MSEK，同比 -32%。但同一份报告里，management 也说 opportunity pipeline YTD +77% 到 $799M，并继续强调 AI data center 的 800G+ pluggables、未来 CPO/NPO 机会。
>
> 这里最容易误判的是：方向对，不等于当季收入兑现；pipeline 很大，不等于 margin、cash flow、customer ramp 已经过关。
>
> 所以看 $CRDO $CIEN $LITE $COHR 这条线，我会把三件事分开：
>
> 1. 现实订单和出货；
> 2. gross margin / customer concentration；
> 3. CPO/NPO 真正商业化时间表。
>
> CPO 是未来方向，但当季财报要先证明“现在能交付什么”。

### Kai - Briefing Block (@briefing_block_)
_Tue Jun 02 20:00:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/briefing_block_/status/2061900664234442795)

> $MRVL  just jumped more than 24% premarket, but the real story is not the Jensen Huang soundbite.
>
> Huang called Marvell the next “trillion-dollar company” at Computex, and the market did what this market does whenever Nvidia anoints a supplier.
>
> It immediately tried to price the endorsement.
>
> But the better read is structural, not promotional.
>
> AI is becoming a data-movement race.
>
> For the last two years, the market has treated AI like a GPU scarcity trade.
>
> That made sense.
>
> Nvidia owned the highest-value layer, hyperscalers were desperate for compute, and every capex guide turned into a referendum on GPU availability.
>
> But the next constraint is different.
>
> Once AI workloads are distributed across enormous clusters, the problem is no longer just how much compute you own.
>
> It is how efficiently thousands of processors can move data, share memory, synchronize work, and keep the cluster from choking on latency.
>
> That is why Marvell matters here.
>
> The cluster is the computer now.
>
> Marvell is not selling a cleaner AI story because it has a better buzzword.
>
> It sits in the layer that connects the machines: high-speed interconnect, Ethernet switching, optical DSP, silicon photonics, custom silicon, and data-center connectivity.
>
> That is exactly where the pain point moves as models get larger and infrastructure gets more distributed.
>
> Marvell’s latest quarter backs up why the stock is getting attention beyond Huang’s comment.
>
> The company reported record fiscal Q1 revenue of $2.418 billion, up 28% year over year, and guided Q2 revenue to $2.7 billion at the midpoint.
>
> Its data-center revenue came in at $1.83 billion, while Marvell said that business is expected to grow about 50% this year.
>
> Nvidia also put real money behind the relationship, investing $2 billion in Marvell as part of a partnership covering NVLink Fusion, custom XPUs, optical interconnect, and silicon photonics.
>
> That matters more than the trillion-dollar line.
>
> The market is not just chasing “the next Nvidia.”
>
> It is trying to figure out which suppliers become unavoidable as AI factories scale.
>
> Bottom line: GPUs started the AI trade, but connectivity may decide the next leg. Marvell is now being priced as one of the companies sitting closest to that bottleneck.

**Media**
- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HJ0Vq2YbEAAL4vT.jpg

### 투자/주식의 생활화 퇴직 오과장 (@datastaion)
_Tue Jun 02 21:14:35 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/datastaion/status/2061919430054117501)

> 마벨(Marvell) CEO, "구리의 벽(Copper Wall)이 랙 내부로 이동하고 있으며, 이를 해결할 유일한 방법은 공동 패키징 광학(CPO)뿐"이라고 밝혀
>
> *마벨 테크놀로지(Marvell Technology)의 CEO 맷 머피(Matt Murphy)는 "AI 인프라의 다음 주요 병목 현상은 연산(Compute)이나 메모리가 아니라, 바로 연결성(Connectivity)
>
> *머피 CEO는 구리(Copper)에서 광학(Optical) 인터커넥트로의 전환이 먼 미래가 아닌 '지금 당장' 일어나고 있으며, 이는 반도체 산업 역사상 전례가 없을 정도로 거대한 수요의 물결을 일으킬 것이라고 말했음.
>
> *구리의 벽(Copper Wall)의 물리학
>
> - 신호가 구리 케이블을 통해 이동할 수 있는 거리는 대역폭에 반비례
>
> - 레인당 100Gbps 수준: 구리 케이블은 약 5미터까지 도달할 수 있어 하나의 랙(Rack) 내부에서 서버들을 연결하기에 충분.
>
> - ​레인당 200Gbps 수준: 그 거리는 약 2.5미터로 줄어들며, 이는 랙의 높이와 내부 라우팅 요구 사항을 감안할 때 딱 한계치에 해당.
>
> - ​레인당 400Gbps 수준: 현재 업계가 나아가고 있는 이 단계에서는 구리선으로 랙 내부를 완전히 연결하는 것이 더 이상 불가능.
>
> *구리의 벽이 한 단계 이동할 때마다, 광학으로 전환해야 하는 연결의 수는 최소 10배 이상 증가. 머피 CEO는 이를 광학 산업의 '수요 폭발'로 묘사.
>
> *​공동 패키징 광학(CPO): 왜 필요한가?
>
> - 랙 내부에서의 전환은 랙과 랙 사이(Inter-rack)에 사용되는 기존의 광학 기술로는 해결할 수 없다. 랙 내부의 연결 수는 랙 간 연결 수보다 약 10배 더 많음. 이 정도의 밀도에서 표준 광학 모듈을 장착하는 것은 전력과 공간 부족으로 인해 물리적으로 불가능.
>
> - ​CPO는 광 엔진(Optical Engines)을 스위치나 연산 패키지에 직접 통합함으로써 이 문제를 해결. 광섬유를 전면 패널이 아닌 칩(Chip)으로 직접 가져오는 방식. 이 기술은 최첨단 CMOS 공정, 실리콘 포토닉스(SiPh), 첨단 패키징, 그리고 광 인터커넥트를 하나의 긴밀하게 통합된 시스템으로 결합.
>
> - 엔비디아(Nvidia)의 베라 루빈(Vera Rubin) 플랫폼이 이미 생산 단계의 첫 CPO 기반 스위치인 '스펙트럼-X 이더넷 포토닉스(Spectrum-X Ethernet Photonics)'를 도입했다는 점을 언급하며, 이러한 전환이 더 이상 이론에 머물지 않는다는 증거로 제시.
>
> *오늘날의 AI 서버는 구리를 통한 고대역폭 통신을 위해 모든 부품이 서로 가까이 위치해야 하므로 CPU, GPU, 맞춤형 가속기, 메모리, 네트워크 인터페이스가 고정된 구성으로 묶여 있음. 이로 인해 연산 장치 대 메모리의 비율이 배포 시점에 고정되어, 어떤 작업(Workload)이 주어지든 시스템의 일부 자원은 항상 유휴 상태(Underutilized)로 남게 됨.
>
> *​그러나 서버 내부의 연결이 광학으로 바뀌면 거리가 더 이상 아키처를 제약하지 않음. 연산, 메모리, 네트워킹을 각각 독립된 풀(Pool)로 분리(Disaggregated)한 뒤, 각 작업이 실제로 필요로 하는 바에 따라 동적으로 구성(Composed)할 수 있게 됨.
>
> *머피 CEO는 "사상 처음으로 설계자들은 인터커넥트(연결)의 한계가 아니라, 오직 모델의 필요에 맞춰 AI 시스템을 설계할 수 있게 될 것입니다"라고 강조.
>
> https://t.co/VkQZnIMKUB

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HJ1n3QKbgAAxnjO.jpg

### Andiamo (@andiamonow)
_Tue Jun 02 21:41:41 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 111 · ↻ 9 · 💬 10 · [open on X](https://x.com/andiamonow/status/2061926249573081367)

> Let me explain what the GlobalFoundries deal actually does for $SIVE — because most retail is reading "partnership" and missing the structural significance.
>
> Reference designs are how foundry ecosystems work.
> When a chip designer wants to build silicon photonics (let's say AMD, Broadcom, or a hyperscaler ASIC team), they don't start from scratch. They start with the foundry's reference design — a pre-validated blueprint for how the components fit together.
> GlobalFoundries' silicon photonics platform is one of the most strategically positioned in the industry. Their SCALE™ optical engine is the foundation for next-generation co-packaged optics.
>
> $SIVE's lasers are now embedded in that reference design.
>
> What this means in practice:
>
> → Every customer who designs silicon photonics on GF's platform starts with $SIVE lasers as the default light source
> → Switching to a non-$SIVE laser requires custom engineering work, custom validation, and supply chain risk
> → $SIVE has effectively become the path of least resistance for the entire GF silicon photonics customer base
>
> The math of why this is different from a normal customer win:
> A typical customer deal = one company buys $SIVE lasers.
>
> A foundry reference design = every customer using that foundry's silicon photonics platform encounters $SIVE lasers in their default design flow.
>
> One captures one customer. The other captures an ecosystem.
>
> The competitive context:
> Coherent, Lumentum, MACOM — these are the larger optical/photonics names retail compares $SIVE to. None of them just got embedded in a major foundry's silicon photonics reference design at the laser layer.
>
> $SIVE just did something its bigger competitors did not.
> And the addressable market GF is targeting? $25B in pluggable optics by 2030.
>
> This is the moat people argued $SIVE didn't have. It just got built. $SIVE

>

>
> Power. Compute. HPC DCs. Photonics. Memory. Networking. Cooling. Models/Apps.
>
> Some of those layers I understand well. Some I understand just enough to be dangerous.
>
> That is why I keep coming back to the most physical parts of the stack.
>
> Land. Power. Buildings. Capacity. Hyperscalers and AI labs who need more compute than the world can currently provide.
>
> That is $IREN to me.
>
> The market spent years treating it like its old business, and probably still does to some extent until AI revenue really shows up.
>
> I think the real story is power-backed infrastructure as compute becomes one of the scarcest resources on earth.
>
> $DGXX is earlier, smaller and more execution heavy, but that is part of the appeal to me.
>
> It feels closer to an early mini $NBIS style setup if they execute.
>
> Same bet: compute demand is a 2 to 3 decade buildout.
>
> The sheer deficit in compute gives me sleep at night comfort. That is why I have sized these names accordingly.
>
> And dare I say it, I think this sector can 100x over the next few decades.
>
> I think we are still early in figuring out who owns the real choke points.
>
> People like @jiahanjimliu, @Agrippa_Inv and @FransBakker9812 are deeper in parts of this stack, but this is how I’m framing it.

### Wind Info (@WindInfoUS)
_Tue Jun 02 23:47:01 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 7 · ↻ 3 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/WindInfoUS/status/2061957791250776371)

> Wind Financial Morning Post: June 3, 2026
>
> Market Brief
>
> The State Council issues the "15th Five-Year Plan for Accelerating Agricultural and Rural Modernization"
>
> China achieves significant breakthrough in optical communication technology
>
> Shanghai establishes a new landmark for the global asset management center: scale to reach RMB 5.5 trillion by 2030
>
> Prospects for U.S.-Iran negotiations remain uncertain, while applications for transit permits through the Strait of Hormuz have opened
>
> The United States lowers import tariffs on selected steel, aluminum, and copper products, and plans to impose a new 25% tariff on Brazil
>
> Global stock markets rose Tuesday, with U.S. markets hitting new highs and South Korea’s market entering the world’s top six largest securities markets
>
> Tiger Brokers: Suspends new position opening and additional positioning for existing investor accounts in all domestic Chinese instruments effective June 12
>
> Microsoft releases seven new AI models to create an integrated “thinking + programming” agent ecosystem
>
> Top Stories
>
> Shanghai has unveiled 21 measures to deepen its construction as a global asset management center, aiming for total asset management scale of 5.4 trillion yuan by 2030, accounting for one-third of the national total. The city will support listings and mergers of technology firms with strong innovation profiles; accelerate the launch of LNG futures and options; prepare for power and computing power futures; promote the listing of Star 50 Index, Shenzhen 100 Index, ChiNext Index futures and options, and government bond options; enhance mechanisms such as “Shanghai-Hong Kong Stock Connect,” “China-Europe Connect,” and “Bond Connect”; and steadily expand institutional openness in the gold market.
>
> Tiger Brokers announced that, to comply with regulatory requirements during the cross-border securities business consolidation period, it will adjust services for existing investor accounts in mainland China starting June 12. Measures include suspending new positions and additional purchases across all securities products, permitting only sell and close-out transactions; and halting inbound fund transfers while maintaining outbound transfer functionality. The company reported first-quarter revenue of $155 million, up 26.3% year-over-year, and operating profit of $48 million, up 17.5%.
>
> According to Iranian sources, the system for applying for vessel transit permits through the Strait of Hormuz has been fully opened, allowing global shipowners and captains to submit applications. Upon approval, vessels will receive transit authorization. Iranian media reported that information exchanges between Iran and the U.S. have been suspended for several days, despite Western media and officials claiming ongoing dialogue. U.S. President Trump stated that talks with Iran continue. U.S. Secretary of State Rubio affirmed that negotiations are still underway but expressed uncertainty over a potential agreement.
>
> Microsoft unveiled seven new AI models at the Build 2026 developer conference, covering full-stack capabilities in reasoning, coding, vision, speech, and multimodal functions. Its flagship reasoning model, MAI-Thinking-1, matched Anthropic’s Claude Sonnet 4.6 on coding benchmarks. The 5-billion-parameter coding model, MAI-Code-1-Flash, targets the GitHub ecosystem. Microsoft also introduced Web IQ, a search engine defined as a “network intelligence layer for AI agents.”
>
> China Macro & Policy
>
> The State Council issued the “15th Five-Year Plan for Accelerating Agricultural and Rural Modernization,” outlining major projects including high-standard farmland construction and cold-chain logistics facilities. The plan promotes diversified food development and the “AI+” agriculture initiative, and identifies key policy measures to cultivate emerging and future industries in agriculture.
>
> National Development and Reform Commission (NDRC) Director Zheng Zhijie convened a meeting with state-owned enterprises to discuss deepening SOE reform, advancing the national unified market, promoting green and low-carbon development, and ensuring energy security. Zheng emphasized enhancing the technological innovation, industrial control, and security support functions of state-owned enterprises.
>
> The Ministry of Finance recently allocated 99.9 billion yuan in childcare subsidies for 2026, a 10.6% increase from last year, to support local governments in providing subsidies to eligible infants. Total fiscal subsidies for the year are projected to reach approximately 110 billion yuan.
>
> The People’s Bank of China reported that in May, standing lending facility (SLF) net injections amounted to 900 million yuan, pledged supplementary lending (PSL) net withdrawals totaled 154.5 billion yuan, and other structural monetary policy tools net injected 112.9 billion yuan; open market treasury purchases resulted in a net injection of 50 billion yuan.
>
> China’s first online tax-refund-for-overseas-tourists store has officially launched in Beijing, alongside the simultaneous activation of centralized tax-refund points in the city’s hotel sector. Overseas visitors can now process tax refunds directly at hotels after online purchases, expanding the scope of tax-refund services.
>
> China Equities Markets
>
> A-share markets climbed modestly, with the SSE Index rising 0.43% to 4,075.10, the Shenzhen Component Index up 1.63%, and the ChiNext Index jumping 2.66%. The Wind All China Index gained 0.75%, with total market turnover reaching 2.81 trillion yuan. The AI computing hardware supply chain strengthened again, with CPO and optical fiber sectors surging. Components, AI PCs, PCBs, and MLCC concepts advanced. Coal stocks maintained strength, while film and theater, and short-form video game concepts declined.
>
> The Hang Seng Index closed up 2.52% at 26,038.32, the Hang Seng Tech Index surged 4.72%, and the Hang Seng China Enterprises Index rose 3%. Technology stocks rallied broadly, with Tencent Holdings soaring over 10%. New energy vehicles and non-ferrous metals led gains, while AI applications and coal stocks declined. Net inflows via the Southbound Stock Connect totaled 2.2 billion Hong Kong dollars, with Tencent Holdings experiencing 2.1 billion Hong Kong dollars in net outflows.
>
> Fund managers led by Jin Zicai announced that to ensure stable fund operations and protect investor interests, subscription limits for multiple funds — including Caichong Growth Optimum, Caichong Value Momentum, Caichong Integrated Circuit Industry, and Caichong Quality Selection — have been lowered to 1,000 yuan.
>
> The Shanghai Stock Exchange website shows that Yushu Technology’s STAR Market IPO status has changed to “submitted for registration.” Yushu Technology’s market director Huang Jiawei revealed that the company’s new-generation humanoid robot reference design, H2 Plus, developed jointly with NVIDIA, will launch in the second half of the year.
>
> China Industry News
>
> China has achieved a major breakthrough in optical communications. The world’s first S+C+L triple-band (short, conventional, and long wavelength) ultra-low-loss multi-core optical cable line has been officially commissioned in Qingdao, Shandong. The single-fiber capacity exceeds five times that of traditional fibers, fully meeting future demands for AI computing and terabit-per-second ultra-high-speed transmission.
>
> Four ministries have launched the “Sword Net 2026” campaign to combat online copyright infringement, with a focus on AI-related copyright issues. The initiative targets violations such as “remixing,” “plagiarism,” and deepfake content in large model training datasets.
>
> According to Centaline Property Research, 141,000 second-hand residential units were sold in 20 cities in May, up 19.3% year-over-year, with the growth rate expanding 6.3 percentage points from April. Beijing and Shanghai recorded 16,000 and 28,000 second-hand home sales respectively, up 12.1% and 30.9% year-over-year, marking the highest May levels in nearly five years. The average second-hand home price across 100 cities fell 0.32% month-over-month, while new home prices rose 0.16%.
>
> Guangzhou’s Nansha District unveiled “Ten Measures” for real estate policy, launching an “old-home-for-new-home” initiative where proceeds from selling an old property can be directly applied toward a new purchase. A subsidy of 1% of the new home’s total price — capped at 20,000 yuan per unit — will be provided, and this can be stacked with municipal subsidies.
>
> The China Passenger Car Association estimated that domestic new energy passenger vehicle wholesale sales reached 1.36 million units in May, up over 11% year-over-year and month-over-month. According to the China Automobile Dealers Association, the automobile consumption index stood at 81 in May, slightly higher than April, suggesting a continued steady upward trend in overall sales for June.
>
> Fintech
>
> Shanghai’s guidelines on deepening its global asset management center status encourage asset managers to leverage AI, blockchain, and big data technologies to accelerate intelligent investment research and advisory services. The city will support the establishment of AI application pilot bases for asset management.
>
> The Hong Kong Securities and Futures Commission issued a circular requiring licensed institutions — particularly online brokers and virtual asset platforms — to strengthen cybersecurity measures to counter emerging threats driven by advanced AI models.
>
> Corporate News & Updates
>
> Sources indicate Tencent has completed prototype testing of its WeChat AI agent and will initiate compliance review procedures as early as this month. Users will be able to use the agent to trigger hundreds of mini-programs for daily tasks such as food ordering. The project has been designated the highest strategic priority. Tencent Cloud has reduced pricing for the DeepSeek-V4 series models by up to 97.5%.
>
> NVIDIA CEO Jensen Huang stated that agent-based AI will fundamentally reshape all AI applications and represent the most important computing transformation over the next decade. Huang also said Marvell Technology will become the next trillion-dollar company. NVIDIA announced full-scale mass production of its NVIDIA Spectrum-X Ethernet silicon photonics technology based on CPO.
>
> Samsung Electronics unveiled its eighth-generation high-bandwidth memory chip, HBM5, and publicly introduced its HPB cooling solution for the first time. Chief Technology Officer Jae-Hyung Song confirmed that HPB technology has been validated on HBM4E chips and will be commercially deployed with HBM5.
>
> Intel CEO Pat Gelsinger, in his Computex 2026 keynote, said agentic AI is reshaping computing demand, and future AI infrastructure will enter a heterogeneous era of co-development among CPUs, GPUs, ASICs, and custom chips. Demand for CPUs in data centers is expected to re-enter a growth cycle.
>
> SK Group Chairman Choi Tae-won said the global shortage of memory chips may persist until 2030, and the company is increasing capital expenditures to bridge the supply-demand gap. SK Hynix plans to double its wafer capacity over the next five years.
>
> ByteDance’s DouBao large model is expected to launch paid content in late June, with plans to integrate e-commerce functions in the third quarter to drive traffic to Douyin Mall. Longer-term operational strategies are not ruled out.
>
> Anthropic announced the expansion of its Glasswing initiative to 150 new partner organizations across more than 15 countries. These institutions will use the Mythos tool to identify software vulnerabilities. New partners span energy, water, healthcare, telecommunications, and hardware industries.
>
> OpenAI released a suite of new plugins for its Codex agent, covering public equity investment, banking, and sales use cases, and plans to introduce legal and corporate finance functions soon. OpenAI also intends to integrate Codex into ChatGPT.
>
> Alibaba Cloud’s Qwen model launched Qwen3.7-Plus, a multimodal large model capable of understanding images and videos, performing deep reasoning, self-programming, tool invocation, validation, and autonomous iteration. It can complete complex, long-horizon tasks such as replicating smartphone apps and desktop software with a single command.
>
> Global Macro & Policy
>
> U.S. President Trump signed an executive order temporarily adjusting import tariffs on certain steel, aluminum, and copper products, effective June 8 through December 31, 2027. Import tariffs on harvesters and other agricultural machinery will be reduced from 25% to 15%, and the domestic content threshold for imported steel, aluminum, and copper will be lowered from 95% to 85%.
>
> The United States plans to impose 25% punitive tariffs on a range of Brazilian imports, including electronic payment services, preferential tariff treatment, intellectual property protections, and ethanol market access. Exemptions include beef, coffee, rare earth minerals, aircraft and aircraft parts, crude oil, fertilizers, and numerous fruits and nuts.
>
> The Canadian government has proposed to the U.S. and Mexico that the USMCA be renewed for 16 years to avoid triggering the agreement’s mandatory annual review process. Under USMCA provisions, the three nations are scheduled to conduct their first joint review in July. The agreement, signed in 2018 and effective since July 2020, is set to expire in 2036.
>
> U.S. officials are reportedly discussing whether to deploy nuclear weapons in additional NATO European countries. The U.S. already deploys nuclear-capable bombers in Belgium, Germany, Italy, the Netherlands, Turkey, and the UK, and has signaled openness to additional deployments.
>
> Hawkish voices within the Federal Reserve are intensifying. Cleveland Fed President Harker said while maintaining current rates remains appropriate, persistent inflation data may soon necessitate policy action — including potential further rate hikes — to counter elevated inflation risks.
>
> Labor market resilience continues to bolster Fed hawkish expectations. U.S. Bureau of Labor Statistics data showed job openings rose to 7.62 million in April, the highest level in two years and well above the 6.87 million forecast. Layoffs fell to 1.692 million, significantly below expectations.
>
> The European Union plans to impose strict eligibility criteria for cloud computing services in key public procurement projects, potentially excluding Amazon, Microsoft, and Google. The proposal aims to reduce EU dependence on U.S. tech products and promote domestic industry development.
>
> Eurostat preliminary data showed euro area CPI rose 3.2% year-over-year in May, up from 3% in April, reinforcing market expectations of a modest ECB rate hike in June.
>
> South Korea’s central bank is poised to raise rates. Statistics Korea reported that May CPI rose 3.1% year-over-year, the largest increase since March 2024. Core CPI increased 2.5%, the highest since February 2024.
>
> The World Meteorological Organization released a report indicating most climate models predict this El Niño will develop into at least a moderate event and may intensify further. Seasonal forecasts suggest most regions will experience above-average temperatures in the coming months.
>
> Global Equity Markets
>
> U.S. major indices closed slightly higher: the Dow Jones Industrial Average rose 0.45% to 51,307.79, the S&P 500 gained 0.13% to 7,609.78, and the Nasdaq Composite edged up 0.03% to 27,093.90 — all closing at record highs. Cisco rose over 5%, Caterpillar gained more than 5%, leading the Dow. The Wind US Magnificent Seven Index declined 1.05%, with Microsoft down over 4% and Google down nearly 4%. The Nasdaq China Golden Dragon Index rose 1.83%, with Canadian Solar up over 12% and Hesai Group up over 8%. Traders closely monitored developments in U.S.-Iran relations and major tech stock performance.
>
> European indices closed higher: Germany’s DAX rose 0.48% to 25,124.17, France’s CAC 40 gained 0.77% to 8,209.09, and the UK’s FTSE 100 climbed 0.33% to 10,373.51. Progress in ceasefire negotiations between Iran and the U.S. lifted risk appetite, but Brent crude breached $95 per barrel, maintaining upward pressure on inflation expectations.
>
> Asia-Pacific markets closed mixed. South Korea’s KOSPI swung sharply — initially surging before plunging more than 3% — and ultimately closed up 0.15% at 8,801.49, setting a new record. South Korea’s total market capitalization surpassed India’s, becoming the world’s sixth-largest stock market. Japan’s Nikkei 225 fell 0.3% to 66,734.24. India’s SENSEX rose 0.52% to 74,649.84.
>
> Andrew Left, founder of the renowned short-selling firm Citron Research, was convicted by a U.S. court of stock manipulation and may face decades in prison. The case could mark a landmark moment for short-sellers globally and reshape regulatory boundaries for short reports and market commentary.
>
> Data from India’s National Securities Depository Limited showed that as of June 1, foreign institutional investors’ net investment in Indian equities totaled 7.3 trillion rupees — the lowest since 2016. Global fund ownership in Indian equities has declined from nearly 20% a decade ago to 15% today.
>
> Bonds
>
> China’s interbank bond market traded in a narrow range, with yields on major government bonds moving slightly in different directions. Treasury futures rallied slightly at the close, with the 10-year contract up 0.06%. Liquidity conditions returned to ample levels as the PBOC conducted 200 million yuan in reverse repo operations, resulting in a net withdrawal of 248.8 billion yuan.
>
> U.S. Treasury yields were mixed: the 2-year yield rose 1.24 basis points to 4.039%, the 3-year yield rose 0.59 basis points to 4.085%, the 5-year yield held steady at 4.163%, the 10-year yield fell 1.18 basis points to 4.439%, and the 30-year yield declined 1.21 basis points to 4.957%.
>
> Commodities
>
> U.S. crude oil futures rose 1.33% to $93.39 per barrel; Brent crude gained 1.01% to $95.94 per barrel. U.S. API crude inventories fell sharply, exceeding market expectations, while geopolitical tensions in the Middle East — including Iran’s suspension of U.S.-Iran talks and its plan to block the Strait of Hormuz — heightened concerns over supply disruptions. The strait handles roughly 20% of global oil shipments, and global crude inventories remain at low levels, jointly supporting higher prices.
>
> International precious metals futures generally rose: COMEX gold futures gained 0.29% to $4,519.20 per ounce, and COMEX silver futures rose 0.25% to $75.44 per ounce. Geopolitical tensions in the Middle East lifted safe-haven demand, while rising U.S. and European rate expectations weighed on market sentiment, creating a tug-of-war.
>
> Most base metals on the LME rose: LME tin climbed 2.88% to $58,280 per ton, LME lead gained 1.52% to $2,037 per ton, LME zinc rose 1.48% to $3,631 per ton, LME aluminum advanced 1.20% to $3,760.50 per ton, LME copper increased 1.10% to $13,983.50 per ton, while LME nickel edged down 0.19% to $19,215 per ton.
>
> The European Central Bank reported that as of the end of 2025, gold accounted for 27% of global official reserve assets, surpassing U.S. Treasuries, which fell to 22%. Gold has become the world’s largest official reserve asset.
>
> Abu Dhabi National Oil Company (ADNOC) revealed plans to construct a refined products pipeline to bypass the Strait of Hormuz. The company is also exploring a new east-west crude oil trunk line that would allow other Gulf producers to route exports through UAE territory, avoiding the strait.
>
> FX & Currency Markets
>
> Onshore renminbi closed at 6.7622 against the U.S. dollar at 16:30, up 28 basis points from the previous close, and settled at 6.7650 in the night session. The PBOC’s mid-rate was set at 6.8187, a 20-basis-point depreciation from the prior day.
>
> At the close of New York trading, the U.S. Dollar Index rose 0.03% to 99.22. Non-U.S. currencies were mixed: the euro fell 0.01% to 1.1631, the pound rose 0.07% to 1.3464, the Australian dollar rose 0.27% to 0.7180, the dollar rose 0.16% against the yen to 159.9295, the dollar fell 0.01% against the Canadian dollar to 1.3839, the dollar rose 0.08% against the Swiss franc to 0.7873, and the offshore renminbi gained 23 basis points to 6.7629.
>
> Japan’s authorities issued a strong signal after record-sized foreign exchange interventions proved ineffective. Finance Minister Kato said the government stands ready to take appropriate action on exchange rates if necessary.
>

> Since $MRVL was up +32%, let me introduce you Taiwan’s Most Direct $MRVL related Stock: LuxNet Corporation 華星光（4979):
>
> Marvell’s push into high-speed Optical DSPs and silicon photonics/CPO solutions for AI data centers has created clear demand for supporting photonic components. LuxNet stands out because of its specific role and long-term relationship with Marvell.
>
> Here’s why the linkage is considered particularly direct:
>
> 1.  Critical Photonic Component Supplier
>
> LuxNet produces InP-based CW Lasers, which serve as the essential external light source in silicon photonics and CPO architectures. These lasers are a key part of enabling Marvell’s advanced Optical DSP platforms.
>
> 2.  Long-Standing Partnership
> The relationship goes back to Marvell’s acquisition of Inphi. 
>
> LuxNet has been a manufacturing and development partner for Marvell’s high-speed optical transceiver modules and continues to work with the company on next-generation solutions.
>
> 3.  Frequently Cited in Market Coverage
>
> When Marvell reports progress in optical or silicon photonics, or when Nvidia deepens cooperation with Marvell, LuxNet is regularly included in analyst and media lists of the most direct Taiwan beneficiaries.
>
> Example: Recent coverage on Nvidia-Marvell silicon photonics collaboration highlighted LuxNet as part of the Taiwan optical supply chain that stands to benefit.
> 4.  Higher Specificity Than Most Peers
> Unlike broader semiconductor or foundry plays, LuxNet’s involvement is more component-specific and tied directly to Marvell’s optical product roadmap, making the supply chain connection more visible and targeted.
>
> This combination of technical role, historical partnership, and consistent market recognition is why LuxNet is often viewed as one of the clearest $MRVL supply chain exposures in Taiwan.

### Ch🅰️rtradamus 🔋 (@Chartradamus)
_Wed Jun 03 20:08:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 20 · ↻ 1 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/Chartradamus/status/2062265269427552310)

> $ANET Fundamental Deep Dive 🟢 Arista Networks
>
> OVERVIEW
>
> Arista Networks operates as a leading provider of networking solutions across AI/HPC infrastructure and routing environments. FY2025 earnings showed significant momentum, with annual revenue of $9B, growing +29% YoY and guiding strongly. Hyperscaler demand and Ethernet fabric expansion delivered the bulk of growth, supported by 400G/800G switches scaling into higher-speed AI clusters. This is only the start of this vertical and will drive growth for years. Excited to see how their 1.6T+ programs and continued AI ramps perform in hyperscaler data centers in 2H 2026 and beyond.
>
> Arista provides the full stack, providing high-performance Ethernet switches with EOS software. This allows ease of virtualization. This company is at the forefront of converting silicon into deployable, rack-ready systems at volume for hyperscalers. They're the pure-play leader enforcing the 1.6T+ photonics wave. It's a significant reason for my comfort in investing in the company as a leveraged AI networking play.
>
> The previous earnings calls confirmed 1.6T+ data center switches are now ready to order, with XPO liquid-cooled pluggable optic modules delivering up to 12.8 Tbps per module. This advancement delivers massive scale and efficiency for hyperscaler AI clusters, addressing power and density limits in next-gen fabrics. The campus and routing segments provide more stable contributions, though with focus shifting toward high-margin AI data center opportunities.
>
> Profitability is set to explode in the years moving forward as AI products mix deeper into the portfolio. Non-GAAP operating margin reached new highs around 47%+ with strong EPS growth. FCF remains exceptional with minimal capital intensity. Competition is present with $NVDA as the behemoth expands into the space with Spectrum-X; however, demand is rampant and Arista is the reliable, proven leader that networking engineers love according to feedback.
>
> ------------------------------------
>
> GROWTH OUTLOOK
>
> $ANET sits at a $220 Billion valuation. Its valuation reflects strong growth expectations with a ~60x Trailing P/E and ~24x P/S Ratio, indicative of the stock sitting at a premium. In my eyes, it's entirely deserved and can easily expand considering it's a extremely high margin business. Leveraging their +25-30% sequential YoY growth, it present a unique opportunity as a pure-play "picks-and-shovels" company.
>
> Arista Networks has consistently outperformed expectations. Management projects robust revenue growth over the next 3–5 years, driven largely by AI data center + Ethernet acceleration. Anticipate a smooth rise in valuation. Their TAM is significant and growing exponentially. It's an extremely comfortable long moving forward. Product roadmaps support this outlook, as shown by their unveiling of 1.6T+ systems and XPO liquid-cooled modules set to hit the the income statement 2H 2026 onwards.
>
> Over FY2026, the company is projected to report ~$11.5B Revenue and $3.60 adjusted EPS annually. This will be followed by even stronger growth in 2027, implying visibility and penetration improvement.
>
> Risks include cyclical demand, supply chain execution, customer concentration, and broader macro slowdowns in tech spending.
>
> ------------------------------------
>
> FAIR VALUATION ESTIMATE
>
> Using an aggregated/blended valuation approach based on many different disciplines of FA (DCF, Relative Multiples, Analysts, etc.),
>
> Current FVE = $240/share
>
> This does not take into account its future prospects and potential for technical momentum to accelerate price far beyond this FVE.
>
> ------------------------------------

> LONG-TERM ESTIMATES
>
> Assuming $ANET consistently meets aggressive growth targets (revenue ramp achieved with margins maintained), this is their potential path forward valuation-wise when using P/E multiples and expected EPS values.
>
> EY2026 = $300+
> EY2027 = $450+

### 독립적 연구 НЕЗАВИСИМЫЕ ИССЛЕДОВАНИЯ (@YusupPulatov)
_Wed Jun 03 21:18:49 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/YusupPulatov/status/2062282883398816193)

> US AFTERMARKET + MACRO RISK SCAN — June 4, 2026
> Matrix Analyst AI | Pulatov Matrix Framework
> OVERVIEW: THE SCHIZOPHRENIC MARKET
> The US market is caught in the most vivid illustration of the matrix's central thesis: two formational forces pulling simultaneously in opposite directions. On one side — Nvidia, valued at $5 trillion, trading around $221–232 range intraday on June 3  (Robinhood) , with the AI/compute mega-cycle accelerating. On the other — WTI futures at $96.02 and Brent at $97.81, rising as the US and Iran traded new strikes, with the Strait of Hormuz still partially blocked  (CNBC) . This is not a "mixed market." This is the rodovye skhvatki formatsii — the birth pangs of the transition, playing out in real time on the ticker.
> OLD FORMATION COLUMN: THERMAL COMBUSTION UNDER SIEGE
> The thermal energy base of late-stage Capitalism is experiencing its most acute stress test since 2008. Roughly 14 million barrels per day of oil supply remain disrupted due to the Strait of Hormuz blockade, with around 850 million barrels of cumulative supply lost over the first two months of the conflict  (ING THINK) . This is not a "geopolitical risk premium" — this is a structural rupture in the energy column of the old formational matrix.
> Brent peaked at $138 per barrel in April — the highest since 2008 — before pulling back to the mid-$90s on ceasefire optimism, creating a violent $90–$100 range with a $138 tail-risk scenario if the strait fully closes  (https://t.co/8hzPgV6wLe) . Saudi Aramco's CEO has reportedly warned the market won't normalize until 2027 if the strait stays shut past mid-June. Capital is pricing a reopening that hasn't happened. That is the definition of fragile.
> The Democracy-Capitalist subject is responding predictably: global oil output expected to fall 6.9 million barrels per day year-on-year in Q2 2026, the largest quarterly decline since COVID-19  (World Bank) . Professional union rights — the freedom level of the old formation — become irrelevant when thermal supply is collapsing. Inflation resets all social contracts.
> NEW FORMATION COLUMN: AI/COMPUTE SIGNAL INTENSIFYING
> While thermal combustion bleeds, the new productive force is printing record valuations. Nvidia at Computex announced Isaac GR00T Reference Humanoid Robot for academic research, DRIVE Hyperion as the global platform for a robotaxi-ready world, Alpamayo 2 Super Open Reasoning Model for robotaxis, and Cosmos 3 as the open frontier foundation model for physical AI  (CNN) — all in a single product cycle. This is not iteration. This is the embodied intelligence column of the new formational matrix going vertical.
> Marvell Technology surged to $290.79, up 32%, after Nvidia CEO highlighted its AI infrastructure role  (Robinhood) . Marvell acquired Celestial AI — a provider of Photonic Fabric technology for next-generation scale-up interconnect — for $3.5 billion in February 2026, with the acquisition expected to accelerate connectivity strategy for next-generation AI and cloud data centers  (sec) . Photonics is the new energy efficiency layer: it sits in the "New energy / power management" column of the transition. This is not a trade — this is capital voting for the next formational architecture.
> CONFLICTS OF TRANSITION
> The matrix identifies three live collision zones right now:
> First, thermal shock vs AI-boom dissociation. The same session saw oil near $96 and Nvidia near $232 all-time-high territory. The old formational capital (energy companies, industrial complex) is being taxed by the Hormuz crisis while new formational capital (AI, semiconductors, optics) breaks records. This is capital migrating between formations in real time.
> Second, capital volatility as formational stress indicator. Brent ran from below $60 at the start of 2026 to a $138 April peak before the May unwind — a range that reflects the system repricing into an entirely different energy regime  (https://t.co/8hzPgV6wLe) .

### 독립적 연구 НЕЗАВИСИМЫЕ ИССЛЕДОВАНИЯ (@YusupPulatov)
_Wed Jun 03 21:19:10 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/YusupPulatov/status/2062282972133486757)

> When the energy foundation of a formation becomes this volatile, it signals the formation is no longer self-sustaining. The thermal combustion era is not ending slowly — it is convulsing.
> Third, Democracy-as-productive-force under geopolitical stress. The US-Iran war is the Democracy column acting out its terminal contradiction: military power deployed to defend the thermal supply chain, while the same democracy-capital system is funding the AI/compute transition that makes that thermal supply chain obsolete. JPMorgan argues that accelerating oil inventory depletion will ultimately force the reopening of the Strait of Hormuz — possibly in June  (CNBC) . Even resolution confirms the diagnosis: the old formation can only survive by emergency management of its own energy base.
> FARWATERS SIGNALS
> In the context of the matrix, the following moves are formational signals, not just price action:
> Marvell at +32% on Nvidia photonics partnership is the advanced packaging / optical interconnect farwater activating. This maps directly to Hanmi Semiconductor's territory: CoWoS, advanced packaging, interconnect density — the hardware layer of the AI productive force.
> Navitas Semiconductor soaring on a partnership with Nvidia, with its 800V-to-6V DC-DC power delivery board displayed at the Nvidia showcase  (CNBC) — this is the power management / new energy efficiency farwater. Navitas operates in the same column as VINA TECH supercapacitors: making compute energy-efficient is how the new formation solves its own energy equation without thermal combustion dependency.
> Coherent getting Nvidia backing for AI datacenter optics expansion is the compute-efficiency signal. Leeno Industrial and Openedges Technology's logic — test sockets for advanced chips, AI IP for efficiency — follows the same directional arrow.
> RISKS BY THE MATRIX
> The thermal supply shock risk remains the single largest formational risk. The World Bank projects Brent averaging $95–$115 in 2026 under current disruption scenarios — 10 to 35 percent above baseline  (World Bank) . This is a direct tax on the old formational capital base and a potential trigger for capital reversal from growth assets if the shock deepens unexpectedly.
> Geopolitical containment risk is secondary: any escalation that draws China into the Hormuz equation — as the largest buyer of Gulf crude — creates a multi-formation crisis that no single policy instrument can contain.
> AI capex reversal risk is the new formation's own vulnerability. Nvidia has declined in 7 of the last 10 sessions  (https://t.co/tF181fPTDi) , signaling that even the new formational flagship is subject to capital rotation when macro fear spikes. NVDA ex-dividend today (June 4, $0.25) is a minor technical event, but the pattern of high-volume selling into strength warns that Capitalist subjects are still booking profits in the transition zone — not yet fully committed to the new paradigm.
> VERDICT: ACCELERATION SCORE — HIGH
> Today's configuration — thermal combustion convulsing at $96 oil, embodied intelligence infrastructure being built at record speed by Nvidia/Marvell/Navitas, and capital visibly migrating between formations — represents one of the highest-velocity transition moments the matrix has recorded.
> The farwaters are not waiting for the Strait of Hormuz to reopen. The new formational productive forces are being built because the old energy base is unstable. That is precisely the dynamic Pulatov's matrix predicts: the new formation does not replace the old at peak stability — it emerges through the crisis of the old.

### Photon Capital (@PhotonCap)
_Wed Jun 03 21:49:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 22 · ↻ 3 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/PhotonCap/status/2062290634963321122)

> ❗ONLY 9 Hours Left❗
>
> [Last Call for Substack/Full article]
>
> Pricing update — effective June 3, 2026 (11:59PM Pacific Time)
>
> PhotonCap started with a simple bet: that there's demand for silicon photonics research that goes deeper than press releases and earnings recaps.
>
> That bet has paid off.
>
> What PhotonCap does differently:
>
> This publication doesn't rely on a single source. Academic conference papers, company PRs, earnings calls, and industry news are cross-referenced and analyzed together. That's how you catch what others miss: when a PR tells one story but the paper tells another.
>
> Here's what that looks like in practice:
>
> Primary source analysis — academic conference papers and journal publications dissected through an investor's lens. Not academic summaries — what each breakthrough means for the supply chain and who captures the value.
>
> Investment maps — supply-chain-level deep dives mapping who actually makes what, from laser sources to optical packaging. The kind of analysis you won't find in sell-side reports.
>
> Portfolio and earnings — portfolio holdings shared on a quarterly or semi-annual basis, alongside earnings analysis that decodes what the numbers actually mean at the product level.
>
> PC101 lecture series — free foundational lectures on silicon photonics, from waveguide physics to PIC design, in English and Korean.
>
> From device physics to public markets — PhotonCap connects the layers that most research treats separately.
>
> Where we stand — and where we're going:
>
> PhotonCap has grown to well over a thousand paid subscribers and ranks #22 on the Substack Top Bestseller list. I'm grateful that this publication is now trusted not only by individual investors, but by institutional investors, hedge funds, and sell-side analysts — as well as fellow research publications including Citrini Research, FundaAI, ChipStrat, Vik's Newsletter, and Jason's Chip, who subscribe as paid members.
>
> Going forward, PhotonCap will expand beyond photonics and optics to cover a broader range of companies — all through the same engineering-first lens. The approach stays the same: primary sources, physics-grounded analysis, and supply chain mapping. The scope gets wider.
>
> New pricing — effective June 3 (11:59 PM, Pacific Time):
>
> Monthly: $50/month (currently $30)
>
> Annual: $500/year (currently $300)
>
> Already a paid subscriber? Your rate is locked in permanently. Nothing changes for you.
>

>
> Content offerings, format, and frequency may evolve over time as PhotonCap grows.

### Armaan Sidhu (@realarmaansidhu)
_Wed Jun 03 21:50:48 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/realarmaansidhu/status/2062290931525566704)

> Nokia is bolting Nvidia GPUs directly into its cell towers, and the reason is a number: 200 milliseconds.
>
> A factory robot can't wait that long for a cloud server to think. So the thinking moves to the tower.
>
> This is the edge-computing thesis finally getting concrete. Instead of routing every AI decision to a distant data center and back, $NOK turns base stations into tiny compute nodes, running the inference where the signal already is. T-Mobile was the first US carrier to pilot it. Nvidia's CEO described a future where every radio network becomes an AI network.
>
> The latency you can't engineer away is the latency of distance.
>
> Underneath the headline, Nokia quietly rebuilt itself. Its $2.3 billion purchase of Infinera turned it from a reseller of someone else's photonics into a vertically integrated optical company with its own chips.
>
> Optical networks grew 20% year over year last quarter. Management raised infrastructure guidance into the teens.
>
> The unglamorous telecom name nobody discussed for a decade is positioning as connective tissue for AI at the edge. Whether the AI-RAN vision pays off is unproven, and the capex is real. But the bet is specific.
>
> The cloud got all the attention. The tower is where the robots actually live.

---

### Armaan Sidhu (@realarmaansidhu)
_Wed Jun 03 21:56:58 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/realarmaansidhu/status/2062292482574946327)

> There's now an ETF for photonics and optics, ticker $LYTE. When a once-obscure corner of tech gets its own ticker, the theme has officially gone mainstream.
>
> That's a signal, and it cuts both ways.
>
> The fair version of the bull case is real: moving data inside AI data centers with light instead of electrons is becoming a genuine bottleneck, and optical components are quietly essential to scaling the whole buildout. Packaging that into one fund lets ordinary investors bet the picks-and-shovels layer under AI without picking one fragile small-cap.
>
> Light is becoming the wiring of the AI era. Someone built a basket for it.
>
> The caution is timing. ETFs tend to launch after a narrative is hot, near the part of the cycle where the easy money already moved. The fund exists because demand for the story exists, and demand for a story usually peaks before the story does.
>
> The product is a thermometer for the hype, not just the trend.
>
> So treat it as both. Photonics genuinely matters to AI infrastructure, and the existence of a dedicated ETF tells you a lot of people already figured that out. Real theme, possibly late entry.
>
> The light's real. Whether you're early to it is the part the ticker can't tell you.
